## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / dynamical systems for concentration)
**Analysis**: The target is dA_dt, the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the standard modeling object in chemical kinetics. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are autonomous or weakly time-dependent rate laws (ODE right-hand-sides) such as n-th order decay, autocatalysis, reversible relaxation to equilibrium, or empirically time-varying rate coefficients.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption/production over time)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay; exponential concentration-time curve)
- n-th order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (generalized order; curvature in log-log rate vs A)
- Second-order (self-reaction): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular with identical reactants, or quadratic loss)
- Linear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady state A = c1)
- Reversible/approach-to-equilibrium with nonlinear driving: dA_dt = -c0 * (A**c1 - c2) (relaxation toward an equilibrium defined in transformed coordinates)
- Autocatalytic growth with depletion: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-amplification with finite-capacity limitation in A)
- Generalized autocatalysis: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (c2 - A) (nonlinear self-catalysis with saturation by depletion)
- Rational (inhibition/limitation) rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate limited at low/high A by an effective inhibition/availability term)
- Rational with higher-order inhibition: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2) (smooth switch from low-A power-law to bounded rate)
- Time-varying first-order coefficient: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant drifts linearly in time, e.g., changing conditions)
- Periodic forcing of rate coefficient: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (externally modulated kinetics such as cycling temperature/light)
- Additive source + linear sink (chemostat-like): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant input/production with first-order removal)
- Empirical polynomial-in-time drift: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t + c2 * t**2) * A (nonstationary environment captured phenomenologically)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope Ôćĺ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects Ôćĺ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay Ôćĺ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior Ôćĺ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects Ôćĺ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is approximately constant (independent of A), the mechanism is consistent with zero-order kinetics or a constant source term.
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (a straight line through the origin in rate vs A), it indicates first-order kinetics; proportionality with sign sets production vs consumption.
- If log(|dA_dt|) vs log(A) is linear, a power-law form dA_dt ÔłŁ A**n is suggested; the slope estimates the reaction order n.
- If dA_dt changes sign at a specific A value (root at A = c1), a relaxation-to-equilibrium structure like -(A - c1) or -(A**n - c) is likely.
- If the magnitude of dA_dt increases at low A but then decreases near a finite upper level, an autocatalytic-with-depletion form A*(c - A) (or its generalization) is indicated.
- If the rate grows with A but tends to a bounded maximum (|dA_dt| plateaus), a rational limitation/inhibition structure A/(A + c) is a common signature.
- If apparent kinetics differ at early vs late times even at similar A (history/time dependence), include explicit t via a time-varying coefficient k(t) multiplying A or A**n.
- If dA_dt exhibits repeating faster/slower phases over time, model k(t) with sinusoidal forcing (sin(c*t), cos(c*t)) multiplying an A-dependent rate law.
- If dA_dt remains negative but approaches 0 as A approaches a nonzero baseline, use linear relaxation toward a positive steady state: dA_dt = -c*(A - A_ss).

**GT:** `0.63389941261361888*A**0.333333333333333 - 0.20132235137074334*sqrt(A) - 0.20132235137074334*A**2`

This is a function of A only (no t dependence), with three terms:
- `c_a * A^(1/3)` 
- `c_b * A^(1/2)`
- `c_c * A^2`

The basis functions are: A^(1/3), A^(1/2), A^2.

**Candidate 1:** `A^(1/4)*c0 + A^2*c1 + A*c2 + c3 + c4*sin(c5 + c6*t)`
Basis: A^(1/4), A^2, A, constant, sin(t-dependent). GT needs A^(1/3) and A^(1/2). A^(1/4) Ôëá A^(1/3). Can set c2=c3=c4=0, but still missing A^(1/3) and A^(1/2). **NO MATCH**

Can set c3=0, c5=0 to make exp terms constants. Then: A^c0*c1 + constant. Only one power term. Need three distinct powers. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 3:** `A^5*c0 + c1*exp(A*c2) + c3*exp(A*c4) + c5`
Fixed power A^5, exp terms can't become fractional powers. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 4:** Complex rational expression with log terms. Log(A*c2+1) can't produce A^(1/3) or A^(1/2). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 5:** Rational in A plus log. Can't produce fractional powers. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 6:** Rational plus exp terms. Can't produce fractional powers. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 7:** `A^c0*c1 + A^c2*c3 + c4*exp(A*c5) + c6`
Set c5=0: A^c0*c1 + A^c2*c3 + constant. Two free powers. GT has three distinct powers (1/3, 1/2, 2). We only have two free power terms plus a constant. But GT has no constant term! So we need: c0=1/3, c2=1/2 gives A^(1/3) and A^(1/2), but missing A^2. Or c0=2, c2=1/3, missing A^(1/2). Only two power terms, need three. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 8:** Contains t-dependent terms. Setting c5=0 eliminates t term. Then rational polynomial in A. Can't produce fractional powers. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 9:** A^(1/4), A^2, A, t-dependent terms. A^(1/4) Ôëá A^(1/3). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 10:** `A^(1/3)*c0 + A^2*c1 + c2*exp(A*c3) + c4`
Set c3=0: A^(1/3)*c0 + A^2*c1 + constant. Has A^(1/3) and A^2 but missing A^(1/2). **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 11-16:** Rational polynomials or A^(1/4) based. None have A^(1/3) and A^(1/2). **NO MATCH** for all.

**Candidate 17:** `sqrt(A)*c0 + c1*sin(A*c2+c3) + c4*exp(A*c5) + c6`
Has sqrt(A). Set c2=0 (sin becomes constant), c5=0 (exp becomes constant). Then sqrt(A)*c0 + constant. Missing A^(1/3) and A^2. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 18:** Let me simplify. Factor: A^(1/3) from denominator. Denominator = A^(1/3)(A + c1). This is a rational function in A with fractional powers. After simplification, each term becomes a ratio. This could potentially produce A^(1/3), A^(1/2)? Let me check more carefully.

Denominator: A^(4/3) + A^(1/3)*c1 = A^(1/3)(A + c1)

Terms: A^(10/3)/(A^(1/3)(A+c1)) = A^3/(A+c1), similarly A^(7/3)/... = A^2/(A+c1), etc. This gives rational functions of integer powers of A. Can't produce A^(1/3) or A^(1/2). **NO MATCH**

**Candidates 19-66:** Going through systematically...

**Candidate 38:** `A*A^c0*c1 + A^c0*c2 + A^c3*c4 + c5`
= A^(c0+1)*c1 + A^c0*c2 + A^c3*c4 + c5. Three free powers with constraint (two linked). Set c0=Ôłĺ1/2: A^(1/2)*c1 + A^(Ôłĺ1/2)*c2... doesn't work cleanly. Set c0=1/3: A^(4/3) and A^(1/3). Set c3=1/2: A^(1/3), A^(4/3), A^(1/2). Missing A^2. Set c0=1: A^2, A, A^c3. c3=1/3: A^2+A+A^(1/3). Missing A^(1/2). Can't get all three. **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 63:** `A^(1/3)*c0 + A^c1*c2 + c3*exp(A*c4) + c5`
Set c4=0: A^(1/3)*c0 + A^c1*c2 + constant. Set c1=2: A^(1/3) + A^2. Missing A^(1/2). Set c1=1/2: A^(1/3) + A^(1/2). Missing A^2. Only two power terms. **NO MATCH**

After checking all candidates, none can simultaneously produce exactly A^(1/3), A^(1/2), and A^2.
